QUESTION: What are the top 5 countries in the world by happiness score, and what is their cost of living index?
TABLES SELECTED: 2019.csv, Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv
KEYWORDS (model raw output): nation, global, well-being, indicator, expense
KEYWORDS (final elaborated): 5, country, world, happiness, score, cost, living, index, nation, global, well, being
MODEL REASONING:
2019.csv provides the most recent happiness scores and country rankings (no year specified by user, so use latest per Priority 5 rule). Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv provides the cost of living index data needed to answer the second part of the question.
DEBUG RAW:
nation, global, well-being, indicator, expense
RETRIES: 0
CODE:
import pandas as pd

# Define file paths
happiness_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv'
cost_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv'

# Load data
df_happiness = pd.read_csv(happiness_path)
df_cost = pd.read_csv(cost_path)

# Sort happiness data by Score descending and select top 5
df_top5 = df_happiness.sort_values(by='Score', ascending=False).head(5)

# Defensive string handling: Normalize country names to lowercase for merging
df_top5['country_key'] = df_top5['Country or region'].str.lower()
df_cost['country_key'] = df_cost['Country'].str.lower()

# Merge tables using the normalized country keys
merged_df = pd.merge(df_top5, df_cost, left_on='country_key', right_on='country_key', how='inner')

# Handle empty results or NaN values in the target metric
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Drop rows where Cost of Living Index is NaN to avoid printing NaN
    merged_df = merged_df.dropna(subset=['Cost of Living Index'])

    if merged_df.empty:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        # Select and print the required columns
        result = merged_df[['Country or region', 'Score', 'Cost of Living Index']]
        print("Top 5 Countries by Happiness Score and Cost of Living Index:")
        print(result.to_string(index=False))

The avocado.csv file is the only dataset containing avocado-specific data with columns for AveragePrice, year, region, and type. This file can provide the average cost of avocados by year and region. The other files are unrelated: 2017.csv contains happiness data, SuperMarket Analysis.csv shows 2019 data from different cities, Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv contains general cost of living indices, and shanghaiData.csv contains university rankings.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# Load the dataset
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/avocado.csv')

# Filter for year 2017
df_2017 = df[df['year'] == 2017]

# Filter for region 'chicago' (case-insensitive)
df_chicago = df_2017[df_2017['region'].str.lower() == 'chicago']

# Filter for type 'organic' (case-insensitive)
df_organic = df_chicago[df_chicago['type'].str.lower() == 'organic']

# Check for empty results
if df_organic.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    avg_price = df_organic['AveragePrice'].mean()
    print(f"The average cost of organic avocados sold in Chicago in 2017 was: {avg_price}")

QUESTION: In the 2024 cost of living data, how many countries have a 'Groceries Index' higher than the 'Rent Index'?
TABLES SELECTED: Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv
KEYWORDS (model raw output): nations, housing, expenditure, statistics, metrics
KEYWORDS (final elaborated): 2024, cost, living, data, country, grocery, index, higher, rent, nations, housing, expenditure
MODEL REASONING:
This file contains the 2024 cost of living data with both Groceries Index and Rent Index columns needed to answer the question. It is the only file required as the comparison is between two columns within the same dataset.
DEBUG RAW:
nations, housing, expenditure, statistics, metrics
RETRIES: 0
CODE:
import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv'

try:
    df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

    # Filter rows where Groceries Index is strictly greater than Rent Index
    # Ensure numeric comparison handles NaN values correctly
    mask = (df['Groceries Index'] > df['Rent Index']) & (df['Groceries Index'].notna()) & (df['Rent Index'].notna())
    
    # Count the number of countries satisfying the condition
    count = mask.sum()

    if count == 0:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        print(f"Number of countries with Groceries Index higher than Rent Index: {int(count)}")

except Exception as e:
    print(f"ERROR: {e}")

The user explicitly asks for data from 2017 regarding well-being and life expectancy. The 2017.csv file contains both Happiness.Score (well-being) and Health..Life.Expectancy. (life expectancy) columns with Country data for the year 2017, making it the only file needed to answer the question.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2017.csv'

try:
    df = pd.read_csv(file_path)
    
    if df.empty:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        # Filter out rows with NaN in the target columns to ensure valid scores
        df_clean = df.dropna(subset=['Happiness.Score', 'Health..Life.Expectancy.'])
        
        if df_clean.empty:
            print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
        else:
            # Sort by both metrics ascending to find the lowest scores
            # Primary sort: Happiness.Score, Secondary sort: Health..Life.Expectancy.
            df_sorted = df_clean.sort_values(by=['Happiness.Score', 'Health..Life.Expectancy.'], ascending=[True, True])
            
            # Select the bottom 1 nation
            result = df_sorted.head(1)
            
            # Print the result
            print(result[['Country', 'Happiness.Score', 'Health..Life.Expectancy.']])
            
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
except Exception as e:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")

QUESTION: Compare the happiness score of Italy in 2015 with its happiness score in 2019. Did it improve?
TABLES SELECTED: 2015.csv, 2019.csv
KEYWORDS (model raw output): index, metric, satisfaction, assess, trend
KEYWORDS (final elaborated): compare, happiness, score, italy, 2015, 2019, did, improve, index, metric, satisfaction, assess

The user needs to compare Italy's happiness score in 2015 with 2019. The 2015.csv file contains happiness data for 2015 with Country and Happiness Score columns. The 2019.csv file contains happiness data for 2019 with Country or region and Score columns. Both files are needed to get the happiness scores for Italy in both years for comparison.
DEBUG RAW:

CODE:
import pandas as pd

path_2015 = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2015.csv'
path_2019 = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv'

df_2015 = pd.read_csv(path_2015)
df_2019 = pd.read_csv(path_2019)

merged_df = pd.merge(
    df_2015,
    df_2019,
    left_on='Country',
    right_on='Country or region',
    suffixes=('_2015', '_2019')
)

italy_data = merged_df[merged_df['Country'].str.lower() == 'italy']

if italy_data.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for Italy in the provided datasets.")
else:
    score_2015 = italy_data['Happiness Score_2015'].iloc[0]
    score_2019 = italy_data['Score_2019'].iloc[0]

    if pd.isna(score_2015) or pd.isna(score_2019):
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: Missing happiness score data for Italy in one of the years.")
    else:
        if score_2019 > score_2015:
            print(f"Italy's happiness score improved from {score_2015} in 2015 to {score_2019} in 2019.")
        elif score_2019 < score_2015:
            print(f"Italy's happiness score decreased from {score_2015} in 2015 to {score_2019} in 2019.")
        else:
            print(f"Italy's happiness score remained the same at {score_2015} in 2015 and {score_2019} in 2019.")

DATA: 2026-04-16 10:29:38
QUESTION: Which country has the highest score in the world, and what is its local purchasing power index?
TABLES SELECTED: Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv, 2019.csv
KEYWORDS (model raw output): nation, global, metric, ranking, parity
KEYWORDS (final elaborated): country, highest, score, world, local, purchasing, power, index, nation, global, metric, ranking
MODEL REASONING:
Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv contains the Local Purchasing Power Index and Country columns needed for the purchasing power data. 2019.csv contains the happiness scores by country. Since no year was specified in the question, the most recent year (2019) is used. The two files can be joined on the country column to find the country with the highest score and its corresponding purchasing power index.
DEBUG RAW:
nation, global, metric, ranking, parity
RETRIES: 0
CODE:
import pandas as pd

# Define file paths
path_cost_of_living = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv'
path_happiness = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv'

# Load data
df_cost = pd.read_csv(path_cost_of_living)
df_happiness = pd.read_csv(path_happiness)

# Normalize country columns to lowercase to handle potential naming mismatches (case sensitivity)
df_cost['Country'] = df_cost['Country'].str.lower()
df_happiness['Country or region'] = df_happiness['Country or region'].str.lower()

# Merge dataframes on country columns
# Using left_on and right_on to handle different column names
merged_df = pd.merge(df_cost, df_happiness, left_on='Country', right_on='Country or region', how='inner')

# Check if merged dataframe is empty
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Find the country with the highest score
    # Ensure Score is numeric
    merged_df['Score'] = pd.to_numeric(merged_df['Score'], errors='coerce')
    
    # Filter out NaN scores if any
    valid_df = merged_df.dropna(subset=['Score'])
    
    if valid_df.empty:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        # Get the row with the maximum score
        max_score_row = valid_df.loc[valid_df['Score'].idxmax()]
        
        country = max_score_row['Country']
        purchasing_power = max_score_row['Local Purchasing Power Index']
        
        # Check for NaN in purchasing power
        if pd.isna(purchasing_power):
            print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
        else:
            print(f"Country with highest score: {country}")
            print(f"Local Purchasing Power Index: {purchasing_power}")

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
Country with highest score: finland
Local Purchasing Power Index: 118.0
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Finland has the highest score in the world, with a local purchasing power index of 118.0.

DATA: 2026-04-16 10:32:16
QUESTION: Is there a relationship between avocado prices and the happiness of a region?
TABLES SELECTED: avocado.csv, 2019.csv
KEYWORDS (model raw output): correlation, welfare, expenditure, locality, association
KEYWORDS (final elaborated): relationship, avocado, price, happiness, region, correlation, welfare, expenditure, locality, association
MODEL REASONING:
avocado.csv provides avocado price data with region information. 2019.csv provides the most recent happiness data with country/region information. These two files can be joined on region/country to analyze the relationship between avocado prices and happiness.
DEBUG RAW:
correlation, welfare, expenditure, locality, association
RETRIES: 0
CODE:
import pandas as pd

# Define exact file paths as per Data Architect instructions
avocado_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/avocado.csv'
happiness_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv'

# Load data
avocado_df = pd.read_csv(avocado_path)
happiness_df = pd.read_csv(happiness_path)

# Defensive string handling for region names to avoid case-sensitivity mismatches
avocado_df['region'] = avocado_df['region'].astype(str).str.lower().str.strip()
happiness_df['Country or region'] = happiness_df['Country or region'].astype(str).str.lower().str.strip()

# Aggregate avocado prices by region to compare with single-year happiness data
avocado_agg = avocado_df.groupby('region')['AveragePrice'].mean().reset_index()
avocado_agg.columns = ['region', 'AveragePrice']

# Merge tables using left_on and right_on for column name mismatch
merged_df = pd.merge(avocado_agg, happiness_df, left_on='region', right_on='Country or region', how='inner')

# Check for empty results after merge
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Ensure numeric types for correlation
    merged_df['AveragePrice'] = pd.to_numeric(merged_df['AveragePrice'], errors='coerce')
    merged_df['Score'] = pd.to_numeric(merged_df['Score'], errors='coerce')

    # Filter out rows with NaN in the variables of interest
    valid_df = merged_df.dropna(subset=['AveragePrice', 'Score'])

    if valid_df.empty:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No valid numeric data found for correlation calculation")
    else:
        correlation = valid_df['AveragePrice'].corr(valid_df['Score'])
        if pd.isna(correlation):
            print("ERROR_EMPTY: Unable to calculate correlation due to insufficient variance or data")
        else:
            print(f"Correlation between avocado prices and happiness score: {correlation:.4f}")

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
I'm afraid there is no data available to answer that question, as no matching records were found for this specific request.

import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/SuperMarket Analysis.csv'

try:
    df = pd.read_csv(file_path)
    
    # Defensive string handling: convert column values to lowercase for comparison
    filtered_df = df[df['Product line'].str.lower() == 'health and beauty']
    
    # Group by Branch and sum gross income
    result = filtered_df.groupby('Branch')['gross income'].sum().reset_index()
    
    # Handle empty results
    if result.empty:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        print(result)
        
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("ERROR_FILE: File not found")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"ERROR: {str(e)}")

import pandas as pd

TABLES SELECTED: 2018.csv, 2019.csv

KEYWORDS (final elaborated): country, experienced, largest, increase, happiness, score, 2018, 2019, nation, growth, maximum, satisfaction

CODE:
import pandas as pd

path_2018 = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2018.csv'
path_2019 = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv'

df_2018 = pd.read_csv(path_2018)
df_2019 = pd.read_csv(path_2019)

# Merge on Country or region using left_on and right_on to handle potential naming mismatches
df_merged = pd.merge(df_2018, df_2019, left_on='Country or region', right_on='Country or region', suffixes=('_2018', '_2019'))

# Calculate the increase in happiness score
df_merged['Score_Increase'] = df_merged['Score_2019'] - df_merged['Score_2018']

# Filter for positive increases to identify the largest increase
df_positive_increase = df_merged[df_merged['Score_Increase'] > 0]

# Handle empty results or NaN cases
if df_positive_increase.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Find the row with the maximum increase
    max_increase_row = df_positive_increase.loc[df_positive_increase['Score_Increase'].idxmax()]
    print(f"Country: {max_increase_row['Country or region']}, Increase: {max_increase_row['Score_Increase']}")

Country: Burundi, Increase: 0.8700000000000001

DATA: 2026-04-16 14:34:57
QUESTION: Among the top 20 happiest countries in 2019, which country has the lowest 'Groceries Index'?
TABLES SELECTED: 2019.csv, Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv
KEYWORDS (model raw output): nations, metrics, indicators, rankings, minimum
KEYWORDS (final elaborated): 20, happiest, country, 2019, lowest, grocery, index, nations, metrics, indicators, rankings, minimum
MODEL REASONING:
Need 2019.csv for top 20 happiest countries in 2019 and Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv for Groceries Index data. These two files can be joined on country names to answer the question.
DEBUG RAW:
nations, metrics, indicators, rankings, minimum
RETRIES: 0
CODE:
import pandas as pd

# Load the datasets using exact paths
df_happiness = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')
df_cost = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# Filter top 20 happiest countries
df_happiness_top20 = df_happiness[df_happiness['Overall rank'] <= 20]

# Normalize country names for merging to handle potential mismatches
df_happiness_top20['country_key'] = df_happiness_top20['Country or region'].str.lower()
df_cost['country_key'] = df_cost['Country'].str.lower()

# Merge the datasets
merged_df = pd.merge(df_happiness_top20, df_cost, left_on='country_key', right_on='country_key', suffixes=('_happiness', '_cost'))

# Check for empty results
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Check if Groceries Index column exists and has valid values
    if 'Groceries Index' not in merged_df.columns:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: Groceries Index column not found")
    else:
        # Filter out NaNs if any before finding min
        valid_df = merged_df.dropna(subset=['Groceries Index'])
        if valid_df.empty:
            print("ERROR_EMPTY: No valid Groceries Index values found")
        else:
            # Find the row with the minimum Groceries Index
            min_row = valid_df.loc[valid_df['Groceries Index'].idxmin()]
            print(f"Country: {min_row['Country or region']}, Groceries Index: {min_row['Groceries Index']}")

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
Country: Czech Republic, Groceries Index: 44.4
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the information provided, the Czech Republic has the lowest Groceries Index at 44.4 among the top 20 happiest countries in 2019.

KEYWORDS (final elaborated): 5, country, world, happiness, score, cost, living, index, nations, satisfaction, rating, budget

2019.csv contains happiness scores with country data (most recent year available per MISSING OR UNSPECIFIED YEARS RULE). import pandas as pd

# Define paths
happiness_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv'
cost_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv'

# Load data
df_happiness = pd.read_csv(happiness_path)
df_cost = pd.read_csv(cost_path)

# Sort happiness by score descending and get top 5
df_happiness_sorted = df_happiness.sort_values(by='Score', ascending=False).head(5)

# Create lowercase versions of country columns for merging to handle case sensitivity
df_happiness_sorted['Country_or_region_lower'] = df_happiness_sorted['Country or region'].str.lower()
df_cost['Country_lower'] = df_cost['Country'].str.lower()

# Merge with cost of living data
merged_df = pd.merge(df_happiness_sorted, df_cost, left_on='Country_or_region_lower', right_on='Country_lower', how='left')

# Select relevant columns for output (original names)
result = merged_df[['Country or region', 'Score', 'Cost of Living Index']]

# Check for empty results or NaNs in the cost of living index
if result.empty or result['Cost of Living Index'].isna().any():
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(result)

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/netflix_titles.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data
# Filter for TV Shows released after 2018
filtered_df = df[(df['release_year'] > 2018) & (df['type'] == 'TV Show')]

# Group by country and count
country_counts = filtered_df.groupby('country').size().reset_index(name='count')

# Sort by count descending and get top 5
top_5_countries = country_counts.sort_values(by='count', ascending=False).head(5)

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if top_5_countries.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(top_5_countries)

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df_2018 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2018.csv')
df_2019 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Merge the two datasets on the country name to align scores
merged_df = pd.merge(df_2018, df_2019, on='Country or region', suffixes=('_2018', '_2019'))

# Calculate the increase in happiness score

# Sort by the increase in descending order to find the largest increase

# Get the top result
result = merged_df.iloc[0]

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(f"Country: {result['Country or region']}")
    print(f"Increase: {result['Increase']}")

DATA: 2026-04-16 15:47:45
QUESTION: Among the top 20 happiest countries in 2019, which country has the lowest 'Groceries Index'?
TABLES SELECTED: 2019.csv, Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv
KEYWORDS (model raw output): ranking, nation, basket, satisfaction, metric
KEYWORDS (final elaborated): 20, happiest, country, 2019, lowest, grocery, index, ranking, nation, basket, satisfaction, metric
MODEL REASONING:
Need 2019.csv to identify the top 20 happiest countries in 2019, and Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv to get the Groceries Index values for those countries. Both files are required to join on country name and answer the question.
DEBUG RAW:
ranking, nation, basket, satisfaction, metric
RETRIES: 0
CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df_happiness = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')
df_cost = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter top 20 happiest countries (Overall rank <= 20)
top_20_happy = df_happiness[df_happiness['Overall rank'] <= 20]

# Normalize country names for merging to handle potential case/whitespace differences
# Rule 4: Use .str.lower()
top_20_happy['country_key'] = top_20_happy['Country or region'].str.strip().str.lower()
df_cost['country_key'] = df_cost['Country'].str.strip().str.lower()

# Merge the dataframes
merged_df = pd.merge(top_20_happy, df_cost, left_on='country_key', right_on='country_key', how='inner')

# Check for empty results
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Filter out NaN Groceries Index if any
    valid_df = merged_df.dropna(subset=['Groceries Index'])
    
    if valid_df.empty:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No valid Groceries Index values found")
    else:
        # Find the row with the lowest Groceries Index
        min_row = valid_df.loc[valid_df['Groceries Index'].idxmin()]
        print(min_row[['Country or region', 'Groceries Index']])

Country or region    Czech Republic
Groceries Index                44.4
Name: 19, dtype: object

    (df['type'].str.lower() == 'movie') &

]

    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    rating_counts = filtered_df['rating'].value_counts()
    most_common_rating = rating_counts.index[0]
    print(most_common_rating)

QUESTION: What is the title of the longest 'Movie' (in minutes) released on Netflix in the year 2020?
TABLES SELECTED: netflix_titles.csv
KEYWORDS (final elaborated): title, longest, movie, minute, released, netflix, year, 2020
MODEL REASONING:
The user question is about Netflix movies released in 2020. The netflix_titles.csv file contains the necessary columns including title, duration, and release_year which are needed to find the longest movie from 2020. The cwurData.csv file is about universities and patents and is completely unrelated to Netflix content, so it should be excluded.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/netflix_titles.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data
# Filter for Movies
df_movies = df[df['type'].str.lower() == 'movie']

# Filter for release year 2020
df_2020 = df_movies[df_movies['release_year'] == 2020]

# Function to parse duration to minutes
def parse_duration(duration):
    if pd.isna(duration):
        return 0
    duration_str = str(duration).strip()
    if 'h' in duration_str:
        parts = duration_str.split('h')
        hours = int(parts[0])
        minutes_part = parts[1].split('m')[0].strip()
        minutes = int(minutes_part)
        return hours * 60 + minutes
    else:
        # Assume format like "45m"
        minutes = int(duration_str.replace('m', ''))
        return minutes

df_2020['duration_minutes'] = df_2020['duration'].apply(parse_duration)

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if df_2020.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Find the row with the maximum duration
    longest_movie = df_2020.loc[df_2020['duration_minutes'].idxmax()]
    print(longest_movie['title'])

QUESTION: What is the title of the longest 'Movie' (in minutes) released on Netflix in the year 2020?
TABLES SELECTED: netflix_titles.csv
KEYWORDS (final elaborated): title, longest, movie, minute, released, netflix, year, 2020
MODEL REASONING:
The netflix_titles.csv file contains all necessary columns (title, duration, release_year) to identify the longest Netflix movie from 2020. The cwurData.csv file is about university rankings and is completely unrelated to Netflix content, so it should be excluded.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/netflix_titles.csv')

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Filter for Movies and Year 2020
df_filtered = df[df['type'].str.lower() == 'movie']
df_filtered = df_filtered[df_filtered['release_year'] == 2020]

# Function to parse duration string to minutes
def parse_duration(duration):
    if pd.isna(duration):
        return 0
    duration = str(duration)
    # Normalize 'h' and 'm' to uppercase for easier splitting
    duration = duration.replace('h', 'H').replace('m', 'M')
    parts = duration.split()
    total_minutes = 0
    for part in parts:
        if 'H' in part:
            total_minutes += int(part.replace('H', '')) * 60
        elif 'M' in part:
            total_minutes += int(part.replace('M', ''))
    return total_minutes

# Apply parsing
df_filtered['duration_minutes'] = df_filtered['duration'].apply(parse_duration)

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if df_filtered.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Find the row with the maximum duration
    longest_movie = df_filtered.loc[df_filtered['duration_minutes'].idxmax()]
    print(longest_movie['title'])

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/netflix_titles.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter for Movies and release year 2020
# Apply str.lower() per Rule 4
filtered_df = df[(df['type'].str.lower() == 'movie') & (df['release_year'] == 2020)]

# Check if filtered data is empty
if filtered_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Parse duration to numeric minutes
    def parse_duration(duration):
        if pd.isna(duration) or str(duration).strip() == '':
            return 0
        duration_str = str(duration)
        if 'h' in duration_str:
            parts = duration_str.split('h')
            minutes = parts[1].split('m')[0].strip()
            return int(minutes)
        else:
            minutes = duration_str.replace('m', '').strip()
            return int(minutes)
    
    filtered_df['duration_minutes'] = filtered_df['duration'].apply(parse_duration)
    
    # Sort by duration descending and get the top title
    longest_movie = filtered_df.loc[filtered_df['duration_minutes'].idxmax(), 'title']
    
    # 3. Check for empty results and Print
    if pd.isna(longest_movie):
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        print(longest_movie)

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/cwurData.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter for Top 100 universities
top_100_df = df[df['world_rank'] <= 100]

# Count appearances per country
country_counts = top_100_df.groupby('country').size()

# Find the country with the highest count
if country_counts.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    result = country_counts.idxmax()
    max_count = country_counts.max()
    print(f"Country with highest total number of university appearances in Top 100: {result}")
    print(f"Total appearances: {max_count}")

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter for Mega names (case-insensitive)
mega_df = df[df['Name'].str.lower().str.contains('mega', na=False)]

# Filter for non-Mega names
non_mega_df = df[~df['Name'].str.lower().str.contains('mega', na=False)]

# Calculate averages
mega_avg = mega_df['Total'].mean()
non_mega_avg = non_mega_df['Total'].mean()

# Calculate difference
difference = mega_avg - non_mega_avg

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if mega_df.empty or non_mega_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(f"Difference in average 'Total' stats: {difference}")

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/netflix_titles.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Filter for TV Shows using defensive filtering (lowercase)
tv_shows_df = df[df['type'].str.lower() == 'tv show']

# Handle cast column: replace NaN with empty string to prevent split errors
tv_shows_df['cast'] = tv_shows_df['cast'].fillna('')

# Split cast by comma and explode to get one row per actor
actors_df = tv_shows_df.assign(cast_list=tv_shows_df['cast'].str.split(',')).explode('cast_list')
actors_df = actors_df.rename(columns={'cast_list': 'actor'})

# Clean actor names (strip whitespace)
actors_df['actor'] = actors_df['actor'].str.strip()

# Filter out empty strings if any remain after split
actors_df = actors_df[actors_df['actor'].str.len() > 0]

# Count frequency
actor_counts = actors_df['actor'].value_counts()

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if actor_counts.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    most_frequent_actor = actor_counts.idxmax()
    count = actor_counts.max()
    print(f"Most frequent actor: {most_frequent_actor} with {count} appearances")

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
Most frequent actor: Takahiro Sakurai with 25 appearances
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Takahiro Sakurai is the most frequent actor across all TV shows on Netflix, with a total of 25 appearances.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/SuperMarket Analysis.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data
# Convert Date column to datetime to extract month
df['Date'] = pd.to_datetime(df['Date'])

# Extract month as integer
df['month'] = df['Date'].dt.month

# Group by month and calculate total gross income
monthly_totals = df.groupby('month')['gross income'].sum()

# Sort by total income descending to find the highest
monthly_totals = monthly_totals.sort_values(ascending=False)

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if monthly_totals.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Get the month with the highest total
    highest_month = monthly_totals.index[0]
    print(highest_month)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
1
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
The raw result is:
1

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/cwurData.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter for universities containing 'technology' or 'institute' (case-insensitive)
# Use na=False to handle potential missing values in the institution column
filtered_df = df[df['institution'].str.lower().str.contains('technology|institute', na=False)]

# Count unique universities
unique_count = filtered_df['institution'].nunique()

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if unique_count == 0:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(unique_count)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
84
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
According to the CWUR dataset, there are 84 unique universities that contain either 'Technology' or 'Institute' in their names.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data
# Filter for Type 1 == 'Water' using .str.lower() as per rules
filtered_df = df[df['Type 1'].str.lower() == 'water']

# Count occurrences of each Type 2
type2_counts = filtered_df['Type 2'].value_counts()

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if filtered_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    most_common_type2 = type2_counts.index[0]
    print(f"The most common 'Type 2' is '{most_common_type2}'")

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/SuperMarket Analysis.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Filter for Health and beauty product line using str.lower()
df_filtered = df[df['Product line'].str.lower() == 'health and beauty']

# Filter for Female and Male genders using str.lower()
df_filtered = df_filtered[(df_filtered['Gender'].str.lower() == 'female') | (df_filtered['Gender'].str.lower() == 'male')]

# Calculate average sales per gender
avg_spending = df_filtered.groupby('Gender')['Sales'].mean()

# Extract averages for Female and Male
female_avg = avg_spending.get('female', 0)
male_avg = avg_spending.get('male', 0)

# Determine if Female average is greater than Male average
# Check if both genders are present to avoid incorrect comparisons with defaults
if 'female' in avg_spending and 'male' in avg_spending:
    result = female_avg > male_avg
else:
    result = False

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if df_filtered.empty or pd.isna(result):
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(result)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
False
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
The answer is False, meaning Female customers do not spend more on average per transaction than Male customers in the Health and beauty product line.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df_happiness = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2018.csv')
df_cost = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Filter for Italy in both datasets using case-insensitive matching
italy_happiness = df_happiness[df_happiness['Country or region'].str.lower() == 'italy']
italy_cost = df_cost[df_cost['Country'].str.lower() == 'italy']

# Merge the filtered dataframes to align the records for Italy
merged_df = pd.merge(
    italy_happiness,
    italy_cost,
    left_on='Country or region',
    right_on='Country',
    how='inner'
)

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for Italy in the provided datasets")
else:
    score = merged_df['Score'].iloc[0]
    cost_index = merged_df['Cost of Living Index'].iloc[0]
    
    if pd.isna(cost_index) or cost_index == 0:
        print("ERROR_CALC: Cost of Living Index is missing or zero for Italy")
    else:
        ratio = score / cost_index
        print(f"Ratio of Score to Cost of Living Index for Italy: {ratio}")

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
Ratio of Score to Cost of Living Index for Italy: 0.10676156583629892
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the 2018 report, the ratio of Italy's Happiness Score to its Cost of Living Index is 0.10676156583629892.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df_2018 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2018.csv')
df_2019 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Rename columns to avoid conflicts when merging
df_2018 = df_2018.rename(columns={'Overall rank': 'rank_2018'})
df_2019 = df_2019.rename(columns={'Overall rank': 'rank_2019'})

# Merge on country name
merged_df = pd.merge(df_2018, df_2019, on='Country or region', how='inner')

# Calculate rank change (increase in rank number = drop in ranking)
merged_df['rank_change'] = merged_df['rank_2019'] - merged_df['rank_2018']

# Filter for countries where rank increased (drop in ranking)
dropped_df = merged_df[merged_df['rank_change'] > 0]

# Find the country with the biggest drop (largest rank_change)
if dropped_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No countries had a drop in rank from 2018 to 2019")
else:
    result = dropped_df.loc[dropped_df['rank_change'].idxmax()]
    print(result[['Country or region', 'rank_2018', 'rank_2019', 'rank_change']])

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
Country or region    Malaysia
rank_2018                  35
rank_2019                  80
rank_change                45
Name: 34, dtype: object
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Malaysia had the biggest drop in its overall rank from 2018 to 2019, falling from 35th to 80th place.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
netflix_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/netflix_titles.csv')
cost_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Count total titles per country
country_counts = netflix_df.groupby('country', as_index=False).size()

# Filter countries that produced more than 500 total titles
high_volume_countries = country_counts[country_counts['size'] > 500]

# Normalize country names to lowercase for consistent joining
high_volume_countries['country'] = high_volume_countries['country'].str.lower()
cost_df['Country'] = cost_df['Country'].str.lower()

# Merge the filtered countries with the cost of living data
merged_df = pd.merge(high_volume_countries, cost_df, left_on='country', right_on='Country', how='inner')

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    avg_rent_index = merged_df['Rent Index'].mean()
    print(avg_rent_index)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
23.650000000000002
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
The average Rent Index for countries that produced more than 500 total titles on Netflix is 23.65.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data
# Filter out Legendary Pokémon
non_legendary_df = df[~df['Legendary']]

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if non_legendary_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No non-legendary Pokémon found.")
else:
    # Calculate average speed per generation
    avg_speed_by_gen = non_legendary_df.groupby('Generation')['Speed'].mean()

    # Find the generation with the highest average speed
    # Sort descending to ensure we get the max
    sorted_avg = avg_speed_by_gen.sort_values(ascending=False)
    
    if not sorted_avg.empty:
        highest_avg_row = sorted_avg.index[0]
        highest_avg_speed = sorted_avg.iloc[0]
        
        # Print the result
        print(f"Generation: {highest_avg_row}, Average Speed: {highest_avg_speed}")
    else:
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No valid speed data found after grouping.")

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
Generation: 1, Average Speed: 71.0875
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the data provided, Generation 1 has the highest average speed of 71.0875.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/netflix_titles.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter for TV Shows only
tv_shows = df[df['type'].str.lower() == 'tv show']

# Extract and split cast column
# Handle NaN values by replacing with empty string before splitting
cast_cleaned = tv_shows['cast'].fillna('').str.split(',')

# Flatten the list of lists
cast_list = [actor for actors in cast_cleaned for actor in actors]

# Create a DataFrame to count frequencies
cast_df = pd.DataFrame({'actor': cast_list})

# Count frequency of each actor
actor_counts = cast_df['actor'].value_counts()

# Get the most frequent actor
most_frequent_actor = actor_counts.idxmax()
count = actor_counts.max()

# Check for empty results
if len(actor_counts) == 0:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(f"Most frequent actor: {most_frequent_actor} with {count} appearances")

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
Most frequent actor:  with 350 appearances
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
The raw result is:
Most frequent actor:  with 350 appearances

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/SuperMarket Analysis.csv')

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Convert Date to datetime to extract month
df['Date'] = pd.to_datetime(df['Date'])
df['month'] = df['Date'].dt.month

# Group by month and sum gross income
monthly_income = df.groupby('month')['gross income'].sum()

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if monthly_income.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    max_month = monthly_income.idxmax()
    print(max_month)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
1
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
The data shows that month 1 generated the highest total gross income across all branches.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/cwurData.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter for 'Technology' or 'Institute' (case-insensitive)
# Using vectorized string methods with na=False to handle potential missing values
mask = df['institution'].str.lower().str.contains('technology', na=False) | \
       df['institution'].str.lower().str.contains('institute', na=False)
    
filtered_df = df[mask]

# Count unique universities
unique_count = filtered_df['institution'].nunique()

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if filtered_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(unique_count)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
84
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the data provided, there are 84 unique universities in the CWUR dataset that contain the word 'Technology' or 'Institute' in their names.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data
# Filter for Type 1 == 'Water' using .str.lower() as per rules
filtered_df = df[df['Type 1'].str.lower() == 'water']

# Group by Type 2 and count occurrences
type2_counts = filtered_df.groupby('Type 2').size()

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if filtered_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
elif type2_counts.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No Type 2 found for Water Pokémon")
else:
    most_common_type2 = type2_counts.idxmax()
    print(f"The most common 'Type 2' is '{most_common_type2}'")

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
The most common 'Type 2' is 'Ground'
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
According to the data, Ground is the most common second type for Pokémon that have Water as their first type.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/SuperMarket Analysis.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter for 'Health and beauty' product line
df_filtered = df[df['Product line'].str.lower() == 'health and beauty']

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if df_filtered.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Calculate average sales for Female and Male
    female_avg = df_filtered[df_filtered['Gender'].str.lower() == 'female']['Sales'].mean()
    male_avg = df_filtered[df_filtered['Gender'].str.lower() == 'male']['Sales'].mean()

    # Compare averages
    result = female_avg > male_avg

    if pd.isna(result):
        print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
    else:
        print(result)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
False
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the data, the answer is False, meaning Female customers do not spend more on average per transaction than Male customers in the Health and beauty product line.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
happiness_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2018.csv')
cost_of_living_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter for Italy in both datasets using case-insensitive matching
italy_happiness = happiness_df[happiness_df['Country or region'].str.lower() == 'italy']
italy_cost_of_living = cost_of_living_df[cost_of_living_df['Country'].str.lower() == 'italy']

# Merge the dataframes on country name
merged_df = pd.merge(italy_happiness, italy_cost_of_living, 
                     left_on='Country or region', 
                     right_on='Country', 
                     how='inner')

# Calculate the ratio of Score to Cost of Living Index
if not merged_df.empty:
    merged_df['Ratio'] = merged_df['Score'] / merged_df['Cost of Living Index']
    result = merged_df['Ratio'].iloc[0]
else:
    result = None

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if result is not None:
    print(result)
else:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
0.10676156583629892
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
In the 2018 report, the ratio of Italy's Happiness Score to its Cost of Living Index is approximately 0.1068.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df_2018 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2018.csv')
df_2019 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Rename columns to avoid conflicts after merge
df_2018 = df_2018.rename(columns={'Overall rank': 'rank_2018', 'Country or region': 'country'})
df_2019 = df_2019.rename(columns={'Overall rank': 'rank_2019', 'Country or region': 'country'})

# Merge the two datasets on country
merged_df = pd.merge(df_2018, df_2019, on='country', how='inner')

# Calculate rank drop (increase in rank number = drop in ranking)
merged_df['rank_drop'] = merged_df['rank_2019'] - merged_df['rank_2018']

# Filter for countries that had a drop (positive rank_drop)
dropped_df = merged_df[merged_df['rank_drop'] > 0]

# Sort by rank_drop descending to find the biggest drop
dropped_df = dropped_df.sort_values('rank_drop', ascending=False)

# Get the top result
result = dropped_df.iloc[0]

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if dropped_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(result[['country', 'rank_2018', 'rank_2019', 'rank_drop']])

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
country      Malaysia
rank_2018          35
rank_2019          80
rank_drop          45

FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Malaysia had the biggest drop in its overall rank from 2018 to 2019, falling 45 positions from 35 to 80.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
netflix_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/netflix_titles.csv')
cost_of_living_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Normalize country names for joining to handle case sensitivity
netflix_df['country_lower'] = netflix_df['country'].str.lower()
cost_of_living_df['country_lower'] = cost_of_living_df['Country'].str.lower()

# Count total titles per country
country_counts = netflix_df.groupby('country_lower').size().reset_index(name='total_titles')

# Filter countries with more than 500 titles
high_volume_countries = country_counts[country_counts['total_titles'] > 500]

# Merge with Cost of Living data
merged_df = pd.merge(high_volume_countries, cost_of_living_df, left_on='country_lower', right_on='country_lower', how='inner')

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    avg_rent_index = merged_df['Rent Index'].mean()
    print(avg_rent_index)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
23.650000000000002
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
The average Rent Index for countries that produced more than 500 total titles on Netflix is 23.65.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/cwurData.csv')

# 2. Process data (filter for year 2014 and top 50 quality_of_education)
filtered_df = df[(df['year'] == 2014) & (df['quality_of_education'] <= 50)]

# Count unique countries
country_count = filtered_df['country'].nunique()

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if filtered_df.empty or country_count == 0:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(country_count)

9
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
In 2014, nine countries had at least one university in the top 50 for quality of education.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv')

# 2. Process data (exclude Legendary and calculate average speed by Generation)
non_legendary_pokemon = df[~df['Legendary']]
avg_speed_by_generation = non_legendary_pokemon.groupby('Generation')['Speed'].mean()
highest_speed_generation = avg_speed_by_generation.sort_values(ascending=False).head(1)

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if highest_speed_generation.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(highest_speed_generation)

Generation
1    71.0875
Name: Speed, dtype: float64
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the data provided, Generation 1 has the highest average speed of 71.0875.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
happiness_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')
cost_of_living_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# 2. Process data - normalize country names for joining
happiness_df['Country or region'] = happiness_df['Country or region'].str.strip()
cost_of_living_df['Country'] = cost_of_living_df['Country'].str.strip()

# Merge on country names (case-insensitive join)
merged_df = pd.merge(
    happiness_df,
    cost_of_living_df,
    left_on='Country or region',
    right_on='Country',
    how='inner',
    suffixes=('_happiness', '_cost')
)

# Sort by happiness score (descending) and get top 5
top_5_happiest = merged_df.nlargest(5, 'Score')[['Country or region', 'Score', 'Cost of Living Index']]

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if top_5_happiest.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(top_5_happiest)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
Country or region  Score  Cost of Living Index
0           Finland  7.769                  63.2
1           Denmark  7.600                  72.3
2            Norway  7.554                  76.0
3           Iceland  7.494                  83.0
4       Netherlands  7.488                  63.1
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Finland leads the pack with a happiness score of 7.769 and a cost of living index of 63.2, followed by Denmark, Norway, Iceland, and the Netherlands with scores of 7.600, 7.554, 7.494, and 7.488, and cost of living indices of 72.3, 76.0, 83.0, and 63.1 respectively.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
happiness_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')
cost_of_living_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Normalize country names for joining to handle potential case/whitespace differences
happiness_df['Country'] = happiness_df['Country or region'].str.strip().str.lower()
cost_of_living_df['Country'] = cost_of_living_df['Country'].str.strip().str.lower()

# Merge on the normalized country column
merged_df = pd.merge(happiness_df, cost_of_living_df, on='Country', how='inner')

# Filter for happiness score above 6 and LPI below 50
filtered_df = merged_df[
    (merged_df['Score'] > 6) & 
    (merged_df['Local Purchasing Power Index'] < 50)
]

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if filtered_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(len(filtered_df))

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
12
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
There are 12 countries that have a happiness score above 6 and a Local Purchasing Power Index below 50.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
path_happiness = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2018.csv'
path_cost = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv'

df_happiness = pd.read_csv(path_happiness)
df_cost = pd.read_csv(path_cost)

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Identify top 10 happiest countries based on Overall rank
top_10_happiness = df_happiness.sort_values('Overall rank').head(10)

# Normalize country names for merging to handle case sensitivity (Rule 4)
top_10_happiness['country_key'] = top_10_happiness['Country or region'].str.lower()
df_cost['country_key'] = df_cost['Country'].str.lower()

# Merge the dataframes on the normalized country keys
merged_df = pd.merge(top_10_happiness, df_cost, left_on='country_key', right_on='country_key', how='inner')

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if merged_df.empty or pd.isna(merged_df['Restaurant Price Index'].mean()):
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    avg_price = merged_df['Restaurant Price Index'].mean()
    print(avg_price)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
69.94000000000001
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
According to the 2018 report, the average Restaurant Price Index for the 10 happiest countries is 69.94.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/SuperMarket Analysis.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data
# Filter for 'Electronic accessories' product line and 'Yangon' city
# Apply defensive filtering using .str.lower()
filtered_df = df[
    (df['Product line'].str.lower() == 'electronic accessories') &
    (df['City'].str.lower() == 'yangon')
]

# Calculate total sum of sales
total_sales = filtered_df['Sales'].sum()

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if filtered_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(total_sales)

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter out Legendary Pokémon
non_legendary_df = df[df['Legendary'] == False]

# Group by Generation and calculate average Speed
avg_speed_by_gen = non_legendary_df.groupby('Generation')['Speed'].mean().reset_index()
avg_speed_by_gen.columns = ['Generation', 'Average_Speed']

# Find the generation with highest average Speed
result = avg_speed_by_gen.loc[avg_speed_by_gen['Average_Speed'].idxmax()]

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if result.empty or pd.isna(result['Average_Speed']):
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(result)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):

Average_Speed    71.0875
Name: 0, dtype: float64
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
When excluding Legendary Pokémon, Generation 1 has the highest average speed, reaching a value of 71.0875.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/cwurData.csv')

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Filter for year 2014
df_2014 = df[df['year'] == 2014]

# Filter for top 50 universities by world_rank
df_top50 = df_2014[df_2014['world_rank'] <= 50]

# Count unique countries
unique_countries = df_top50['country'].nunique()

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if df_top50.empty or unique_countries == 0:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    print(unique_countries)

9
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
In 2014, there were 9 countries that had at least one university in the top 50 for quality of education.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
netflix_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/netflix_titles.csv')
cost_of_living_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Count total titles per country
country_counts = netflix_df.groupby('country').size().reset_index(name='total_titles')

# Filter countries with more than 500 titles
high_volume_countries = country_counts[country_counts['total_titles'] > 500]

# Normalize country names for joining to handle case sensitivity
high_volume_countries['country'] = high_volume_countries['country'].str.lower()
cost_of_living_df['Country'] = cost_of_living_df['Country'].str.lower()

# Merge on country names
merged_df = pd.merge(high_volume_countries, cost_of_living_df, left_on='country', right_on='Country', how='inner')

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    avg_rent_index = merged_df['Rent Index'].mean()
    print(avg_rent_index)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
23.650000000000002
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
For countries that produced more than 500 total titles on Netflix, the average Rent Index is 23.65.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df_2018 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2018.csv')
df_2019 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Rename columns for easier merging
df_2018 = df_2018.rename(columns={'Country or region': 'country_2018'})
df_2019 = df_2019.rename(columns={'Country or region': 'country_2019'})

# Merge on country name
merged = pd.merge(df_2018, df_2019, left_on='country_2018', right_on='country_2019', how='inner')

# Calculate rank difference (2019 rank - 2018 rank)
# A positive difference means rank got worse (bigger number = lower rank)
merged['rank_change'] = merged['Overall rank_x'] - merged['Overall rank_y']

# Filter for countries where rank dropped (rank increased numerically)
# rank_change > 0 means 2019 rank is worse than 2018 rank
dropped = merged[merged['rank_change'] > 0]

# Find the country with the biggest drop (largest rank_change)
if dropped.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No countries had a drop in rank from 2018 to 2019")
else:
    biggest_drop = dropped.loc[dropped['rank_change'].idxmax()]
    print(biggest_drop[['country_2018', 'Overall rank_x', 'Overall rank_y', 'rank_change']])

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
country_2018      Benin
Overall rank_x      136
Overall rank_y      102
rank_change          34
Name: 133, dtype: object
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the provided data, Benin had the biggest drop in its overall rank, with a rank change of 34 positions between 2018 and 2019.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df_2018 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2018.csv')
df_2019 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Rename columns to avoid conflicts when merging
df_2018 = df_2018.rename(columns={'Overall rank': 'rank_2018'})
df_2019 = df_2019.rename(columns={'Overall rank': 'rank_2019'})

# Merge on country name
merged_df = pd.merge(df_2018, df_2019, on='Country or region', how='inner')

# Calculate rank difference (2019 rank - 2018 rank)
# A positive difference means rank increased (drop in ranking)
merged_df['rank_difference'] = merged_df['rank_2019'] - merged_df['rank_2018']

# Filter for countries that had a drop in ranking (positive difference)
dropped_df = merged_df[merged_df['rank_difference'] > 0]

# Sort by rank_difference descending to find the biggest drop
dropped_df = dropped_df.sort_values('rank_difference', ascending=False)

# Get the top result
result = dropped_df.iloc[0]

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if dropped_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No countries found with a drop in ranking from 2018 to 2019")
else:
    if isinstance(result, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(result.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(result)

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
happiness_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2018.csv')
cost_of_living_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Filter for Italy in happiness data (defensive filtering)
italy_happiness = happiness_df[happiness_df['Country or region'].str.lower() == 'italy']

# Filter for Italy in cost of living data (defensive filtering)
italy_cost = cost_of_living_df[cost_of_living_df['Country'].str.lower() == 'italy']

# Merge the two datasets on country name
merged_df = pd.merge(italy_happiness, italy_cost, left_on='Country or region', right_on='Country', how='inner')

# Calculate the ratio
if not merged_df.empty:
    merged_df['Ratio'] = merged_df['Score'] / merged_df['Cost of Living Index']
    result = merged_df['Ratio'].iloc[0]
else:
    result = None

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if merged_df.empty or result is None:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    if isinstance(result, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(result.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(result)

0.10676156583629892
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the data provided, the ratio of the Happiness Score to the Cost of Living Index for Italy in the 2018 report is 0.10676156583629892.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/SuperMarket Analysis.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Filter for 'Health and beauty' product line (case-insensitive)
df_filtered = df[df['Product line'].str.lower() == 'health and beauty']

# Filter for Male and Female genders (case-insensitive)
df_filtered = df_filtered[df_filtered['Gender'].str.lower().isin(['male', 'female'])]

# Group by Gender and calculate mean Sales
avg_spending = df_filtered.groupby('Gender')['Sales'].mean()

# Check for empty results and Print
if df_filtered.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Extract values for comparison
    if 'female' in avg_spending and 'male' in avg_spending:
        result = avg_spending['female'] > avg_spending['male']
    else:
        result = False
    
    if isinstance(result, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(result.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(result)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
False
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the data provided, the answer is False, meaning Female customers do not spend more on average per transaction than Male customers in the Health and beauty product line.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data
# Filter for Type 1 == 'Water' using .str.lower() as per rules
water_pokemon = df[df['Type 1'].str.lower() == 'water']

# Group by Type 2 and count occurrences
type2_counts = water_pokemon.groupby('Type 2', as_index=False).size()

# Sort by count descending and select the top result
most_common = type2_counts.sort_values('size', ascending=False).head(1)

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if most_common.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    if isinstance(most_common, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(most_common.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(most_common)

Type 2  size
Ground    10
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the data provided, Ground is the most common Type 2 for Water-type Pokémon, appearing 10 times.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/SuperMarket Analysis.csv')

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
df['Date'] = pd.to_datetime(df['Date'])
df['month'] = df['Date'].dt.month
monthly_income = df.groupby('month')['gross income'].sum()
max_month_row = monthly_income.sort_values(ascending=False).head(1)

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if max_month_row.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    result = max_month_row.index[0]
    print(result)

1
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the data provided, month 1 generated the highest total gross income across all branches.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/netflix_titles.csv')

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Filter for TV Shows using .str.lower() as per Rule 4
tv_shows_df = df[df['type'].str.lower() == 'tv show']

# Process cast column
# Drop nulls to avoid errors in string operations
cast_series = tv_shows_df['cast'].dropna()

# Split cast by comma to separate actors
cast_split = cast_series.str.split(',')

# Explode to create one row per actor
actors_df = cast_split.explode('cast')

# Clean actor names: strip whitespace and convert to lowercase (Rule 4)
actors_df['cast'] = actors_df['cast'].str.strip().str.lower()

# Filter out empty strings that might result from splitting
actors_df = actors_df[actors_df['cast'] != '']

# Count frequencies of each actor
actor_counts = actors_df['cast'].value_counts()

# Get the most frequent actor
result = actor_counts.head(1)

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if result.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    if isinstance(result, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(result.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(result)

import pandas as pd

file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/netflix_titles.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# Filter for TV Shows
tv_shows = df[df['type'] == 'TV Show']

# Clean cast column: strip whitespace and lowercase
tv_shows['cast'] = tv_shows['cast'].str.strip().str.lower()

# Split cast into individual actors
tv_shows['cast'] = tv_shows['cast'].str.split(',')

# Explode to create one row per actor
actors_df = tv_shows.explode('cast')

# Remove rows where cast is NaN or empty
actors_df = actors_df[actors_df['cast'].notna() & (actors_df['cast'] != '')]

# Strip individual actor names to remove spaces from split
actors_df['cast'] = actors_df['cast'].str.strip()

# Count frequencies
actor_counts = actors_df['cast'].value_counts()

# Get the most frequent actor
most_frequent = actor_counts.head(1)

print(most_frequent)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
cast
takahiro sakurai    25
Name: count, dtype: int64
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the data, Takahiro Sakurai is the most frequent actor across all TV Shows on Netflix, appearing 25 times in the cast.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/SuperMarket Analysis.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data
# Filter for 'Normal' customers and 'Food and beverages' product line
# Apply .str.lower() as per defensive filtering rules
filtered_df = df[(df['Customer type'].str.lower() == 'normal') & (df['Product line'].str.lower() == 'food and beverages')]

# Calculate total Tax 5%
total_tax = filtered_df['Tax 5%'].sum()

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if filtered_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    if isinstance(total_tax, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(total_tax.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(total_tax)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
1015.355
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
The data shows that the total 'Tax 5%' paid by Normal customers for items in the Food and beverages product line is 1015.355.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df_2019 = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2019.csv')
df_cost = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Filter 2019 data for Happiness Score > 6.0
df_2019_filtered = df_2019[df_2019['Score'] > 6.0]

# Align column names for merging ('Country or region' vs 'Country')
df_2019_filtered = df_2019_filtered.rename(columns={'Country or region': 'Country'})

# Merge the two dataframes
merged_df = pd.merge(df_2019_filtered, df_cost, on='Country', how='inner')

# Select relevant columns and sort by Local Purchasing Power Index descending
result = merged_df.sort_values(by='Local Purchasing Power Index', ascending=False).head(5)

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if result.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    if isinstance(result, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(result.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(result)

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
pokemon_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')
avocado_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/avocado.csv')

# 2. Process data - Check if 'Total' column exists in either dataframe
# Since neither table contains Pokémon data, we need to check available columns
available_columns = set(pokemon_df.columns) | set(avocado_df.columns)

# Check if 'Total' column exists in any available dataframe
has_total = 'Total' in available_columns

# Check if any column contains 'Name' or similar for filtering
has_name = any('name' in col.lower() for col in available_columns)

# Since neither table contains Pokémon data with 'Total' stats, we cannot perform the requested calculation
# Print available columns for debugging
print("Available columns in Cost of Living table:", list(pokemon_df.columns))
print("Available columns in Avocado table:", list(avocado_df.columns))

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if not has_total:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No 'Total' column found in available tables. Neither table contains Pokémon data.")
elif not has_name:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No 'Name' column found in available tables. Cannot filter by Pokémon names.")
else:
    # This would be the calculation if data existed
    mega_pokemon = pokemon_df[pokemon_df['Name'].str.lower().str.contains('mega', na=False)]
    non_mega_pokemon = pokemon_df[~pokemon_df['Name'].str.lower().str.contains('mega', na=False)]
    
    mega_avg = mega_pokemon['Total'].mean()
    non_mega_avg = non_mega_pokemon['Total'].mean()
    difference = mega_avg - non_mega_avg
    
    if isinstance(difference, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(difference.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(difference)

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv')

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Filter for names containing 'Mega' (case-insensitive)
mega_df = df[df['Name'].str.lower().str.contains('mega', na=False)]
# Filter for names NOT containing 'Mega'
non_mega_df = df[~df['Name'].str.lower().str.contains('mega', na=False)]

# Calculate averages
mega_avg = mega_df['Total'].mean()
non_mega_avg = non_mega_df['Total'].mean()

# Calculate difference
difference = mega_avg - non_mega_avg

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if mega_df.empty or non_mega_df.empty or pd.isna(difference):
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    result = difference
    if isinstance(result, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(result.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(result)

190.44
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
The difference in the average 'Total' stats between Pokémon whose name contains the word 'Mega' and those that do not is 190.44.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
cwur_df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/cwurData.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter for Top 100 universities
top_100_df = cwur_df[cwur_df['world_rank'] <= 100]

# Group by country and count appearances
country_counts = top_100_df.groupby('country').size().reset_index(name='total_appearances')

# Find the country with the highest total number of appearances
result = country_counts.loc[country_counts['total_appearances'].idxmax()]

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if result.empty or pd.isna(result['total_appearances']):
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    if isinstance(result, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(result.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(result)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
USA
223
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
Based on the data provided, the USA has the highest total number of university appearances in the Top 100, with 223 appearances recorded across all years.

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
file_path = '/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Pokemon.csv'
df = pd.read_csv(file_path)

# 2. Process data (apply Architect's logic)
# Filter for Water-type (Type 1) and non-Legendary
# Apply .str.lower() as per defensive filtering rule
water_mask = df['Type 1'].str.lower() == 'water'
non_legendary_mask = ~df['Legendary']

filtered_df = df[water_mask & non_legendary_mask]

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if not filtered_df.empty:
    # Sort by Total descending and select the top row
    top_pokemon = filtered_df.loc[filtered_df['Total'].idxmax()]
    result = top_pokemon[['Name', 'Total']]
    
    if isinstance(result, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(result.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(result)
else:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")

                  640

The raw result is:

import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/SuperMarket Analysis.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter for 'Health and beauty' product line (case-insensitive)
df_filtered = df[df['Product line'].str.lower() == 'health and beauty']

# Group by branch and sum gross income
result = df_filtered.groupby('Branch')['gross income'].sum().reset_index()

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if result.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    if isinstance(result, (pd.Series, pd.DataFrame)):
        print(result.to_string(index=False))
    else:
        print(result)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
Branch  gross income
  Alex       599.893
 Cairo       951.460
  Giza       791.206
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
The total gross income for the 'Health and beauty' product line is 599.893 at the Alex branch, 951.460 at Cairo, and 791.206 at Giza.

CODE:
import pandas as pd

# 1. Load data
df_happiness = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/2018.csv')
df_cost = pd.read_csv('/home/gabriele.martinelli/LakeGen/LakeGen_T/Data/data_csv/Cost_of_Living_Index_by_Country_2024.csv')

# 2. Process data
# Filter top 10 happiest countries based on Overall rank
top_10_happy = df_happiness[df_happiness['Overall rank'] <= 10]

# Normalize country names for merging (Rule 4: ALWAYS use .str.lower())
# Apply strip to remove potential whitespace
top_10_happy['Country'] = top_10_happy['Country or region'].str.lower().str.strip()
df_cost['Country'] = df_cost['Country'].str.lower().str.strip()

# Merge the dataframes on the normalized country column
merged_df = pd.merge(top_10_happy, df_cost, left_on='Country', right_on='Country', how='inner')

# 3. Check for empty results and Print
if merged_df.empty:
    print("ERROR_EMPTY: No matching records found for those filters")
else:
    # Calculate average Restaurant Price Index
    avg_restaurant_price = merged_df['Restaurant Price Index'].mean()
    print(avg_restaurant_price)

RAW OUTPUT (Phase 4):
69.94000000000001
FINAL RESULT (Phase 5):
According to the 2018 report, the average Restaurant Price Index for the 10 happiest countries is 69.94.
